<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Four-vector</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>

<p>In <a href="/wiki/Special_relativity" title="Special relativity">special relativity</a>, a <b>four-vector</b> (also known as a 4-vector)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> is an object with four components, which transform in a specific way under <a href="/wiki/Lorentz_transformation" title="Lorentz transformation">Lorentz transformations</a>. Specifically, a four-vector is an element of a four-dimensional <a href="/wiki/Vector_space" title="Vector space">vector space</a> considered as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Representation_space" title="Representation space">representation space</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Representation_theory_of_the_Lorentz_group" title="Representation theory of the Lorentz group">standard representation</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Lorentz_group" title="Lorentz group">Lorentz group</a>, the (½,½) representation. It differs from a <a href="/wiki/Euclidean_vector" title="Euclidean vector">Euclidean vector</a> in how its magnitude is determined. The transformations that preserve this magnitude are the Lorentz transformations, which include <a href="/wiki/Rotation_group_SO(3)" title="Rotation group SO(3)">spatial rotations</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lorentz_transformation#Boost_in_the_x-direction" title="Lorentz transformation">boosts</a> (a change by a constant velocity to another <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inertial_reference_frame" title="Inertial reference frame">inertial reference frame</a>), and <a href="/wiki/T-symmetry" title="T-symmetry">temporal</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/P-symmetry" title="P-symmetry">spatial</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inversion_in_a_point#Inversion_with_respect_to_the_origin" title="Inversion in a point">inversions</a>.</p>
<p>Four-vectors describe, for instance, position <span class="texhtml"><i>x</i><sup><i>μ</i></sup></span> in spacetime modeled as <a href="/wiki/Minkowski_space" title="Minkowski space">Minkowski space</a>, a particle's <a href="/wiki/Four-momentum" title="Four-momentum">four-momentum</a> <span class="texhtml"><i>p</i><sup><i>μ</i></sup></span>, the amplitude of the <a href="/wiki/Electromagnetic_four-potential" title="Electromagnetic four-potential">electromagnetic four-potential</a> <span class="texhtml"><i>A</i><sup><i>μ</i></sup>(<i>x</i>)</span> at a point <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">x</span> in spacetime, and the elements of the subspace spanned by the <a href="/wiki/Gamma_matrices" title="Gamma matrices">gamma matrices</a> inside the <a href="/wiki/Representation_theory_of_the_Lorentz_group#Induced_representations" title="Representation theory of the Lorentz group">Dirac algebra</a>.</p>
<p>The Lorentz group may be represented by 4×4 matrices <span class="texhtml">Λ</span>. The action of a Lorentz transformation on a general <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Contravariant_vector" title="Contravariant vector">contravariant</a> four-vector <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">X</span> (like the examples above), regarded as a column vector with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cartesian_coordinates" title="Cartesian coordinates">Cartesian coordinates</a> with respect to an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inertial_frame#Special_relativity" title="Inertial frame">inertial frame</a> in the entries, is given by</p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mi>X</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi class="MJX-variant" mathvariant="normal">′<!-- ′ --></mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>=</mo>
<mi mathvariant="normal">Λ<!-- Λ --></mi>
<mi>X</mi>
<mo>,</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle X^{\prime }=\Lambda X,}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="X^\prime = \Lambda X," aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0560a70488d8863fd549ae12761530d9ae92b039" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:10.08ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span></dd>
</dl>
<p>(matrix multiplication) where the components of the primed object refer to the new frame. Related to the examples above that are given as contravariant vectors, there are also the corresponding <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Covariant_vector" title="Covariant vector">covariant vectors</a> <span class="texhtml"><i>x</i><sub><i>μ</i></sub></span>, <span class="texhtml"><i>p</i><sub><i>μ</i></sub></span> and <span class="texhtml"><i>A</i><sub><i>μ</i></sub>(<i>x</i>)</span>. These transform according to the rule</p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mi>X</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi class="MJX-variant" mathvariant="normal">′<!-- ′ --></mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>=</mo>
<msup>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<msup>
<mi mathvariant="normal">Λ<!-- Λ --></mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo>−<!-- − --></mo>
<mn>1</mn>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
</mrow>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="normal">T</mi>
</mrow>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mi>X</mi>
<mo>,</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle X^{\prime }={(\Lambda ^{-1})}^{\mathrm {T} }X,}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="X^\prime = {(\Lambda^{-1})}^\mathrm T X," aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/93b04f50f1a57e66e5d61de85078ab84ac6fc79d" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:15.684ex; height:3.676ex;"/></span></dd>
</dl>
<p>where <span class="texhtml"><sup>T</sup></span> denotes the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Matrix_transpose" title="Matrix transpose">matrix transpose</a>. This rule is different from the above rule. It corresponds to the <a href="/wiki/Dual_representation" title="Dual representation">dual representation</a> of the standard representation. However, for the Lorentz group the dual of any representation is <a href="/wiki/Representation_theory_of_the_Lorentz_group#Dual_representations" title="Representation theory of the Lorentz group">equivalent</a> to the original representation. Thus the objects with covariant indices are four-vectors as well.</p>
<p>For an example of a well-behaved four-component object in special relativity that is <i>not</i> a four-vector, see <a href="/wiki/Bispinor" title="Bispinor">bispinor</a>. It is similarly defined, the difference being that the transformation rule under Lorentz transformations is given by a representation other than the standard representation. In this case, the rule reads <span class="texhtml"><i>X</i><sup>′</sup> = Π(Λ)<i>X</i></span>, where <span class="texhtml">Π(Λ)</span> is a 4×4 matrix other than <span class="texhtml">Λ</span>. Similar remarks apply to objects with fewer or more components that are well-behaved under Lorentz transformations. These include <a href="/wiki/Scalar_field" title="Scalar field">scalars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spinor" title="Spinor">spinors</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tensors" title="Tensors">tensors</a> and spinor-tensors.</p>
<p>The article considers four-vectors in the context of special relativity. Although the concept of four-vectors also extends to <a href="/wiki/General_relativity" title="General relativity">general relativity</a>, some of the results stated in this article require modification in general relativity.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notation">Notation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Four-vector&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Notation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The notations in this article are: lowercase bold for <a href="/wiki/Three-dimensional_space" title="Three-dimensional space">three-dimensional</a> vectors, hats for three-dimensional <a href="/wiki/Unit_vector" title="Unit vector">unit vectors</a>, capital bold for <a href="/wiki/Spacetime" title="Spacetime">four dimensional</a> vectors (except for the four-gradient), and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tensor_index_notation" title="Tensor index notation">tensor index notation</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Four-vector_algebra">Four-vector algebra</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Four-vector&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Four-vector algebra">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Four-vectors_in_a_real-valued_basis">Four-vectors in a real-valued basis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Four-vector&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Four-vectors in a real-valued basis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A <b>four-vector</b> <i>A</i> is a vector with a "timelike" component and three "spacelike" components, and can be written in various equivalent notations:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup></p>

<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\begin{aligned}\mathbf {A} &amp;=(A^{0},\,A^{1},\,A^{2},\,A^{3})\\&amp;=A^{0}\mathbf {E} _{0}+A^{1}\mathbf {E} _{1}+A^{2}\mathbf {E} _{2}+A^{3}\mathbf {E} _{3}\\&amp;=A^{0}\mathbf {E} _{0}+A^{i}\mathbf {E} _{i}\\&amp;=A^{\alpha }\mathbf {E} _{\alpha }\\&amp;=A^{\mu }\end{aligned}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle {\begin{aligned}\mathbf {A} &amp;=(A^{0},\,A^{1},\,A^{2},\,A^{3})\\&amp;=A^{0}\mathbf {E} _{0}+A^{1}\mathbf {E} _{1}+A^{2}\mathbf {E} _{2}+A^{3}\mathbf {E} _{3}\\&amp;=A^{0}\mathbf {E} _{0}+A^{i}\mathbf {E} _{i}\\&amp;=A^{\alpha }\mathbf {E} _{\alpha }\\&amp;=A^{\mu }\end{aligned}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/3f5b88d95f5ec51a135b578fa1664450725df43d" style="vertical-align: -7.338ex; width:37.02ex; height:15.843ex;"/></span></dd>
</dl>
<p>where in the last form the magnitude component and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Basis_vector" title="Basis vector">basis vector</a> have been combined to a single element.</p>
<p>The upper indices indicate <a href="/wiki/Covariance_and_contravariance_of_vectors" title="Covariance and contravariance of vectors">contravariant</a> components. Here the standard convention is that Latin indices take values for spatial components, so that <i>i</i> = 1, 2, 3, and Greek indices take values for space <i>and time</i> components, so <i>α</i> = 0, 1, 2, 3, used with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Summation_convention" title="Summation convention">summation convention</a>. The split between the time component and the spatial components is a useful one to make when determining contractions of one four vector with other tensor quantities, such as for calculating Lorentz invariants in inner products (examples are given below), or <a href="/wiki/Raising_and_lowering_indices" title="Raising and lowering indices">raising and lowering indices</a>.</p>
<p>In special relativity, the spacelike basis <b>E</b><sub>1</sub>, <b>E</b><sub>2</sub>, <b>E</b><sub>3</sub> and components <i>A</i><sup>1</sup>, <i>A</i><sup>2</sup>, <i>A</i><sup>3</sup> are often <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cartesian_coordinates" title="Cartesian coordinates">Cartesian</a> basis and components:</p>

<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\begin{aligned}\mathbf {A} &amp;=(A_{t},\,A_{r},\,A_{\theta },\,A_{z})\\&amp;=A_{t}\mathbf {E} _{t}+A_{r}\mathbf {E} _{r}+A_{\theta }\mathbf {E} _{\theta }+A_{z}\mathbf {E} _{z}\\\end{aligned}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\begin{aligned}{\mathbf  {A}}&amp;=(A_{t},\,A_{r},\,A_{\theta },\,A_{z})\\&amp;=A_{t}{\mathbf  {E}}_{t}+A_{r}{\mathbf  {E}}_{r}+A_{\theta }{\mathbf  {E}}_{\theta }+A_{z}{\mathbf  {E}}_{z}\\\end{aligned}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/74c2679cc8cb000c00505d2b9ed770834e186320" style="vertical-align: -2.338ex; width:36.196ex; height:5.843ex;"/></span></dd>
</dl>
<p>or any other <a href="/wiki/Orthogonal_coordinates" title="Orthogonal coordinates">orthogonal coordinates</a>, or even general <a href="/wiki/Curvilinear_coordinates" title="Curvilinear coordinates">curvilinear coordinates</a>. Note the coordinate labels are always subscripted as labels and are not indices taking numerical values. In general relativity, local curvilinear coordinates in a local basis must be used. Geometrically, a four-vector can still be interpreted as an arrow, but in spacetime - not just space. In relativity, the arrows are drawn as part of <a href="/wiki/Minkowski_diagram" title="Minkowski diagram">Minkowski diagram</a> (also called <i>spacetime diagram</i>). In this article, four-vectors will be referred to simply as vectors.</p>

<p>The relation between the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Covariant_vector" title="Covariant vector">covariant</a> and contravariant coordinates is through the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Minkowski_metric" title="Minkowski metric">Minkowski</a> <a href="/wiki/Metric_tensor" title="Metric tensor">metric tensor</a> (referred to as the metric), <i>η</i> which <a href="/wiki/Raising_and_lowering_indices" title="Raising and lowering indices">raises and lowers indices</a> as follows:</p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<p>so that:</p>

<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbf {A} ={\begin{pmatrix}A_{0}&amp;A_{1}&amp;A_{2}&amp;A_{3}\end{pmatrix}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt=" \mathbf{A} = \begin{pmatrix} A_0 &amp; A_1 &amp; A_2 &amp; A_3 \end{pmatrix} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/e2b6e0d76ff889ea4754c63d4cf290004d85e791" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:25.949ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span></dd>
</dl>
<p>The motivation for the above conventions are that the inner product is a scalar, see below for details.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lorentz_transformation">Lorentz transformation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Four-vector&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Lorentz transformation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Lorentz_transformation" title="Lorentz transformation">Lorentz transformation</a></div>
<p>Given two inertial or rotated <a href="/wiki/Frame_of_reference" title="Frame of reference">frames of reference</a>, a four-vector is defined as a quantity which transforms according to the <a href="/wiki/Lorentz_transformation" title="Lorentz transformation">Lorentz transformation</a> matrix <b>Λ</b>:</p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="bold">A</mi>
</mrow>
<mo>′</mo>
</msup>
<mo>=</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="bold">Λ<!-- Λ --></mi>
</mrow>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="bold">A</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbf {A} '={\boldsymbol {\Lambda }}\mathbf {A} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbf{A}'=\boldsymbol{\Lambda}\mathbf{A}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/89ffa3a01578ae9eb6c46ad82dad166f899ab731" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:9.745ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span></dd>
</dl>
<p>In index notation, the contravariant and covariant components transform according to, respectively:</p>
<dl>

<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>μ<!-- μ --></mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<msup>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
</mrow>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>ν<!-- ν --></mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {A'}^{\mu }=\Lambda ^{\mu }{}_{\nu }A^{\nu }\,,\quad {A'}_{\mu }=\Lambda _{\mu }{}^{\nu }A_{\nu }}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{A'}^\mu = \Lambda^\mu {}_\nu A^\nu \,,\quad {A'}_\mu = \Lambda_\mu {}^\nu A_\nu" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/771dcc2629e7c1b70395cfc33be6644705d7c06d" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:30.984ex; height:3.343ex;"/></span></dd>
</dl>
<p>in which the matrix <b>Λ</b> has components Λ<i><sup>μ</sup><sub>ν</sub></i> in row <i>μ</i> and column <i>ν</i>, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inverse_matrix" title="Inverse matrix">inverse matrix</a> <b>Λ</b><sup>−1</sup> has components Λ<i><sub>μ</sub><sup>ν</sup></i> in row <i>μ</i> and column <i>ν</i>.</p>
<p>For background on the nature of this transformation definition, see <a href="/wiki/Tensor#Definition" title="Tensor">tensor</a>. All four-vectors transform in the same way, and this can be generalized to four-dimensional relativistic tensors; see <a href="/wiki/Special_relativity#Transformations_of_physical_quantities_between_reference_frames" title="Special relativity">special relativity</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Pure_rotations_about_an_arbitrary_axis">Pure rotations about an arbitrary axis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Four-vector&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Pure rotations about an arbitrary axis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Pure_boosts_in_an_arbitrary_direction">Pure boosts in an arbitrary direction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Four-vector&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Pure boosts in an arbitrary direction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Standard_conf.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="335" data-file-width="390" height="258" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Standard_conf.png/300px-Standard_conf.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/90/Standard_conf.png 1.5x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Standard_conf.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Standard configuration of coordinate systems; for a Lorentz boost in the <i>x</i>-direction.</div>
</div>
</div>

<p>Where the <a href="/wiki/Rapidity" title="Rapidity">rapidity</a> <i>ϕ</i> expression has been used, written in terms of the <a href="/wiki/Hyperbolic_function" title="Hyperbolic function">hyperbolic functions</a>:</p>

</dl>
<p>This Lorentz matrix illustrates the boost to be a <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hyperbolic_rotation" title="Hyperbolic rotation">hyperbolic rotation</a></i> in four dimensional spacetime, analogous to the circular rotation above in three-dimensional space.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Properties">Properties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Four-vector&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Properties">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Linearity">Linearity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Four-vector&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Linearity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Four-vectors have the same <a href="/wiki/Linear_algebra" title="Linear algebra">linearity properties</a> as <a href="/wiki/Euclidean_vector" title="Euclidean vector">Euclidean vectors</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Three_dimensions" title="Three dimensions">three dimensions</a>. They can be added in the usual entrywise way:</p>

<mo>,</mo>

<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>3</mn>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>

</dl>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Minkowski_tensor">Minkowski tensor</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Four-vector&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Minkowski tensor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spacetime_interval" title="Spacetime interval">spacetime interval</a></div>
<p>Applying the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Minkowski_tensor" title="Minkowski tensor">Minkowski tensor</a> <i>η<sub>μν</sub></i> to two four-vectors <b>A</b> and <b>B</b>, writing the result in <a href="/wiki/Dot_product" title="Dot product">dot product</a> notation, we have, using <a href="/wiki/Einstein_notation" title="Einstein notation">Einstein notation</a>:</p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="bold">A</mi>
</mrow>
<mo>⋅<!-- ⋅ --></mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="bold">B</mi>
</mrow>
<mo>=</mo>
<msup>
<mi>A</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>μ<!-- μ --></mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<msub>
<mi>η<!-- η --></mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>μ<!-- μ --></mi>
<mi>ν<!-- ν --></mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<msup>
<mi>B</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>ν<!-- ν --></mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbf {A} \cdot \mathbf {B} =A^{\mu }\eta _{\mu \nu }B^{\nu }}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbf{A} \cdot \mathbf{B} = A^{\mu} \eta_{\mu \nu} B^{\nu} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f860deabecb13b9370ac15373208a034b14ef8e2" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:17.885ex; height:3.009ex;"/></span></dd>

</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbf{A \cdot B} = \begin{pmatrix} A^0 &amp; A^1 &amp; A^2 &amp; A^3 \end{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \eta_{00} &amp; \eta_{01} &amp; \eta_{02} &amp; \eta_{03} \\ \eta_{10} &amp; \eta_{11} &amp; \eta_{12} &amp; \eta_{13} \\ \eta_{20} &amp; \eta_{21} &amp; \eta_{22} &amp; \eta_{23} \\ \eta_{30} &amp; \eta_{31} &amp; \eta_{32} &amp; \eta_{33} \end{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} B^0 \\ B^1 \\ B^2 \\ B^3 \end{pmatrix} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/2ee1b750f31c24f7ed1aa73a64c5843016a64cf2" style="vertical-align: -5.838ex; width:61.26ex; height:12.843ex;"/></span></dd>
</dl>
<p>in which case <i>η<sub>μν</sub></i> above is the entry in row <i>μ</i> and column <i>ν</i> of the Minkowski metric as a square matrix. The Minkowski metric is not a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Euclidean_metric" title="Euclidean metric">Euclidean metric</a>, because it is indefinite (see <a href="/wiki/Metric_signature" title="Metric signature">metric signature</a>). A number of other expressions can be used because the metric tensor can raise and lower the components of <b>A</b> or <b>B</b>. For contra/co-variant components of <b>A</b> and co/contra-variant components of <b>B</b>, we have:</p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="bold">A</mi>
</mrow>
<mo>⋅<!-- ⋅ --></mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="bold">B</mi>
</mrow>
<mo>=</mo>
<msup>
<mi>A</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>μ<!-- μ --></mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<msub>
<mi>η<!-- η --></mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>μ<!-- μ --></mi>
<mi>ν<!-- ν --></mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<msup>
<mi>B</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>ν<!-- ν --></mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>=</mo>
<msub>
<mi>A</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>ν<!-- ν --></mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<msup>
<mi>B</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>ν<!-- ν --></mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>=</mo>
<msup>
<mi>A</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>μ<!-- μ --></mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<msub>
<mi>B</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>μ<!-- μ --></mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbf {A} \cdot \mathbf {B} =A^{\mu }\eta _{\mu \nu }B^{\nu }=A_{\nu }B^{\nu }=A^{\mu }B_{\mu }}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle \mathbf {A} \cdot \mathbf {B} =A^{\mu }\eta _{\mu \nu }B^{\nu }=A_{\nu }B^{\nu }=A^{\mu }B_{\mu }}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/d6e6e77e2aab622c19ca579c86888ff0dd11a2cf" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:35.842ex; height:3.009ex;"/></span></dd>
</dl>
<p>so in the matrix notation:</p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="bold">A</mi>
<mo>⋅<!-- ⋅ --></mo>
<mi mathvariant="bold">B</mi>
</mrow>
<mo>=</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mrow>
<mo>(</mo>
<mtable columnspacing="1em" rowspacing="4pt">
<mtr>
<mtd>
<msub>
<mi>A</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>0</mn>
</mrow>
</msub>
</mtd>
<mtd>
<msub>
<mi>A</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>1</mn>
</mrow>
</msub>
</mtd>
<mtd>
<msub>

</dl>
<p>which, depending on the case, may be considered the square, or its negative, of the length of the vector.</p>
<p>Following are two common choices for the metric tensor in the <a href="/wiki/Minkowski_space#Standard_basis" title="Minkowski space">standard basis</a> (essentially Cartesian coordinates). If orthogonal coordinates are used, there would be scale factors along the diagonal part of the spacelike part of the metric, while for general curvilinear coordinates the entire spacelike part of the metric would have components dependent on the curvilinear basis used.</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Standard_basis.2C_.28.2B.E2.88.92.E2.88.92.E2.88.92.29_signature">Standard basis, (+−−−) signature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Four-vector&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Standard basis, (+−−−) signature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>

<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbf {A} '\cdot \mathbf {B} '={A'}^{0}{B'}^{0}-{A'}^{1}{B'}^{1}-{A'}^{2}{B'}^{2}-{A'}^{3}{B'}^{3}=C'}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt=" \mathbf{A}'\cdot\mathbf{B}' = {A'}^0 {B'}^0 - {A'}^1 {B'}^1 - {A'}^2 {B'}^2 - {A'}^3 {B'}^3 = C' " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/d09d7ee72979fe630d1d51a16eee2820a3cc2b74" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:52.428ex; height:3.009ex;"/></span></dd>
</dl>
<p>in another frame, in which <i>C</i>′ is the value of the inner product in this frame. Then since the inner product is an invariant, these must be equal:</p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<mi mathvariant="bold">B</mi>
</mrow>
<mo>=</mo>
<msup>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="bold">A</mi>
</mrow>
<mo>′</mo>
</msup>
<mo>⋅<!-- ⋅ --></mo>
<msup>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="bold">B</mi>
</mrow>
<mo>′</mo>
</msup>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbf {A} \cdot \mathbf {B} =\mathbf {A} '\cdot \mathbf {B} '}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt=" \mathbf{A}\cdot\mathbf{B} = \mathbf{A}'\cdot\mathbf{B}' " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/d57b35bc66e57ec21393c25ff7c0b665ad6f57cb" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:15.755ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span></dd>
</dl>
<p>that is:</p>

<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle C=A^{0}B^{0}-A^{1}B^{1}-A^{2}B^{2}-A^{3}B^{3}={A'}^{0}{B'}^{0}-{A'}^{1}{B'}^{1}-{A'}^{2}{B'}^{2}-{A'}^{3}{B'}^{3}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt=" C = A^0 B^0 - A^1 B^1 - A^2 B^2 - A^3 B^3 = {A'}^0 {B'}^0 - {A'}^1 {B'}^1 - {A'}^2 {B'}^2 - {A'}^3{B'}^3 " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/954913e59baf560b0181b162da3bf056b8845898" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:75.847ex; height:3.009ex;"/></span></dd>
</dl>
<p>Considering that physical quantities in relativity are four-vectors, this equation has the appearance of a "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conservation_law_(physics)" title="Conservation law (physics)">conservation law</a>", but there is no "conservation" involved. The primary significance of the Minkowski inner product is that for any two four-vectors, its value is <a href="/wiki/Invariant_(physics)" title="Invariant (physics)">invariant</a> for all observers; a change of coordinates does not result in a change in value of the inner product. The components of the four-vectors change from one frame to another; <b>A</b> and <b>A′</b> are connected by a <a href="/wiki/Lorentz_transformation" title="Lorentz transformation">Lorentz transformation</a>, and similarly for <b>B</b> and <b>B′</b>, although the inner products are the same in all frames. Nevertheless, this type of expression is exploited in relativistic calculations on a par with conservation laws, since the magnitudes of components can be determined without explicitly performing any Lorentz transformations. A particular example is with energy and momentum in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Energy-momentum_relation" title="Energy-momentum relation">energy-momentum relation</a> derived from the <a href="/wiki/Four-momentum" title="Four-momentum">four-momentum</a> vector (see also below).</p>
<p>In this signature we have:</p>

<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Standard_basis.2C_.28.E2.88.92.2B.2B.2B.29_signature">Standard basis, (−+++) signature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Four-vector&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Standard basis, (−+++) signature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>

<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Dual_vectors">Dual vectors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Four-vector&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Dual vectors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>Applying the Minkowski tensor is often expressed as the effect of the <a href="/wiki/Dual_space#Ailinear_products_and_dual_spaces" title="Dual space">dual vector</a> of one vector on the other:</p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="bold">A</mi>
<mo>⋅<!-- ⋅ --></mo>
<mi mathvariant="bold">B</mi>
</mrow>
<mo>=</mo>
<msup>
<mi>A</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo>∗<!-- ∗ --></mo>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="bold">B</mi>
</mrow>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
<mo>=</mo>
<mi>A</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<msub>
<mi></mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>ν<!-- ν --></mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
</mrow>
<msup>
<mi>B</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>ν<!-- ν --></mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>.</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbf {A\cdot B} =A^{*}(\mathbf {B} )=A{_{\nu }}B^{\nu }.}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbf{A \cdot B} = A^*(\mathbf{B}) = A{_\nu}B^{\nu}. " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/fa28b6f01ff2b1bfd2e0a1bf448fa11208ddf910" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:24.813ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span></dd>
</dl>
<p>Here the <i>A<sub>ν</sub></i>s are the components of the dual vector <b>A</b>* of <b>A</b> in the <a href="/wiki/Dual_basis" title="Dual basis">dual basis</a> and called the <a href="/wiki/Covariance_and_contravariance_of_vectors" title="Covariance and contravariance of vectors">covariant</a> coordinates of <b>A</b>, while the original <i>A<sup>ν</sup></i> components are called the <a href="/wiki/Covariance_and_contravariance_of_vectors" title="Covariance and contravariance of vectors">contravariant</a> coordinates.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Four-vector_calculus">Four-vector calculus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Four-vector&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Four-vector calculus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Derivatives_and_differentials">Derivatives and differentials</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Four-vector&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Derivatives and differentials">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In special relativity (but not general relativity), the <a href="/wiki/Derivative" title="Derivative">derivative</a> of a four-vector with respect to a scalar <i>λ</i> (invariant) is itself a four-vector. It is also useful to take the <a href="/wiki/Differential_of_a_function" title="Differential of a function">differential</a> of the four-vector, <i>d</i><b>A</b> and divide it by the differential of the scalar, <i>dλ</i>:</p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<munder>
<mrow>
<mi>d</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="bold">A</mi>
</mrow>
</mrow>
<mtext>differential</mtext>
</munder>
</mrow>
<mo>=</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<munder>
<mfrac>
<mrow>
<mi>d</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="bold">A</mi>
</mrow>
</mrow>
<mrow>
<mi>d</mi>
<mi>λ<!-- λ --></mi>
</mrow>
</mfrac>
<mtext>derivative</mtext>
</munder>
</mrow>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<munder>
<mrow>
<mi>d</mi>
<mi>λ<!-- λ --></mi>
</mrow>
<mtext>differential</mtext>
</munder>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\underset {\text{differential}}{d\mathbf {A} }}={\underset {\text{derivative}}{\frac {d\mathbf {A} }{d\lambda }}}{\underset {\text{differential}}{d\lambda }}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\underset{\text{differential}}{d\mathbf{A}} = \underset{\text{derivative}}{\frac{d\mathbf{A}}{d\lambda}} \underset{\text{differential}}{d\lambda} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/332e1572732f5e6c3084c0995d62f27c64593814" style="vertical-align: -3.838ex; width:26.037ex; height:7.343ex;"/></span></dd>
</dl>
<p>where the contravariant components are:</p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>d</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="bold">A</mi>
</mrow>
<mo>=</mo>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mi>d</mi>
<msup>
<mi>A</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>0</mn>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>,</mo>
<mi>d</mi>
<msup>

<p>In relativistic mechanics, one often takes the differential of a four-vector and divides by the differential in <a href="/wiki/Proper_time" title="Proper time">proper time</a> (see below).</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Fundamental_four-vectors">Fundamental four-vectors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Four-vector&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Fundamental four-vectors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Four-position">Four-position</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Four-vector&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Four-position">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A point in <a href="/wiki/Minkowski_space" title="Minkowski space">Minkowski space</a> is a time and spatial position, called an "event", or sometimes the position four-vector or four-position or 4-position, described in some reference frame by a set of four coordinates:</p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="bold">R</mi>
</mrow>
<mo>=</mo>
<mrow>
<mo>(</mo>
<mi>c</mi>
<mi>t</mi>
<mo>,</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="bold">r</mi>
</mrow>
<mo>)</mo>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbf {R} =\left(ct,\mathbf {r} \right)}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\mathbf  {R}}=\left(ct,{\mathbf  {r}}\right)" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/d15681fe4d61720e3eb1ae7f66291d3ed0e7ad33" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:10.977ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span></dd>
</dl>
<p>where <b>r</b> is the <a href="/wiki/Three-dimensional_space" title="Three-dimensional space">three-dimensional space</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Position_vector" title="Position vector">position vector</a>. If <b>r</b> is a function of coordinate time <i>t</i> in the same frame, i.e. <b>r</b> = <b>r</b>(<i>t</i>), this corresponds to a sequence of events as <i>t</i> varies. The definition <i>R</i><sup>0</sup> = <i>ct</i> ensures that all the coordinates have the same units (of distance).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> These coordinates are the components of the <i>position four-vector</i> for the event. The <i>displacement four-vector</i> is defined to be an "arrow" linking two events:</p>

<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<mo>(</mo>
<mi>c</mi>
<mi mathvariant="normal">Δ<!-- Δ --></mi>

<mo>,</mo>
<mi mathvariant="normal">Δ<!-- Δ --></mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="bold">r</mi>
</mrow>
<mo>)</mo>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \Delta \mathbf {R} =\left(c\Delta t,\Delta \mathbf {r} \right)}</annotation>
</semantics>

<p>When considering physical phenomena, differential equations arise naturally; however, when considering space and <a href="/wiki/Time_derivative" title="Time derivative">time derivatives</a> of functions, it is unclear which reference frame these derivatives are taken with respect to. It is agreed that time derivatives are taken with respect to the <a href="/wiki/Proper_time" title="Proper time">proper time</a> <span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>τ<!-- τ --></mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \tau }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\tau " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/38a7dcde9730ef0853809fefc18d88771f95206c" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.212ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span>. As proper time is an invariant, this guarantees that the proper-time-derivative of any four-vector is itself a four-vector. It is then important to find a relation between this proper-time-derivative and another time derivative (using the <a href="/wiki/Coordinate_time" title="Coordinate time">coordinate time</a> <i>t</i> of an inertial reference frame). This relation is provided by taking the above differential invariant spacetime interval, then dividing by (<i>cdt</i>)<sup>2</sup> to obtain:</p>

</dl>
<p>is the <a href="/wiki/Lorentz_factor" title="Lorentz factor">Lorentz factor</a>. This provides a useful relation between the differentials in coordinate time and proper time:</p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<mi mathvariant="bold">u</mi>

<mi>d</mi>
<mi>τ<!-- τ --></mi>
<mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace>
<mo>.</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle dt=\gamma (\mathbf {u} )d\tau \,.}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt=" dt = \gamma(\mathbf{u})d\tau \,." aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f46a604c2450e82532abea793bf1f15354911728" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:13.267ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span></dd>
</dl>
<p>This relation can also be found from the time transformation in the <a href="/wiki/Lorentz_transformation" title="Lorentz transformation">Lorentz transformations</a>.</p>
<p>Important four-vectors in relativity theory can be defined by applying this differential <span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mfrac>
<mi>d</mi>
<mrow>
<mi>d</mi>
<mi>τ<!-- τ --></mi>
</mrow>
</mfrac>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\frac {d}{d\tau }}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\frac {d}{d\tau }}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/bc7b820089566d6cd0b6de6e95bc6e0a618d00bf" style="vertical-align: -2.005ex; width:3.275ex; height:5.509ex;"/></span>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Four-gradient">Four-gradient</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Four-vector&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Four-gradient">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Considering that <a href="/wiki/Partial_derivative" title="Partial derivative">partial derivatives</a> are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Linear_operator" title="Linear operator">linear operators</a>, one can form a <a href="/wiki/Four-gradient" title="Four-gradient">four-gradient</a> from the partial <a href="/wiki/Time_derivative" title="Time derivative">time derivative</a> <span class="texhtml">∂</span>/<span class="texhtml">∂</span><i>t</i> and the spatial <a href="/wiki/Gradient" title="Gradient">gradient</a> ∇. Using the standard basis, in index and abbreviated notations, the contravariant components are:</p>

<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\begin{aligned}{\boldsymbol {\partial }}&amp;=\left({\frac {\partial }{\partial x_{0}}},\,-{\frac {\partial }{\partial x_{1}}},\,-{\frac {\partial }{\partial x_{2}}},\,-{\frac {\partial }{\partial x_{3}}}\right)\\&amp;=(\partial ^{0},\,-\partial ^{1},\,-\partial ^{2},\,-\partial ^{3})\\&amp;=\mathbf {E} _{0}\partial ^{0}-\mathbf {E} _{1}\partial ^{1}-\mathbf {E} _{2}\partial ^{2}-\mathbf {E} _{3}\partial ^{3}\\&amp;=\mathbf {E} _{0}\partial ^{0}-\mathbf {E} _{i}\partial ^{i}\\&amp;=\mathbf {E} _{\alpha }\partial ^{\alpha }\\&amp;=\left({\frac {1}{c}}{\frac {\partial }{\partial t}},\,-\nabla \right)\\&amp;=\left({\frac {\partial _{t}}{c}},-\nabla \right)\\&amp;=\mathbf {E} _{0}{\frac {1}{c}}{\frac {\partial }{\partial t}}-\nabla \\\end{aligned}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle {\begin{aligned}{\boldsymbol {\partial }}&amp;=\left({\frac {\partial }{\partial x_{0}}},\,-{\frac {\partial }{\partial x_{1}}},\,-{\frac {\partial }{\partial x_{2}}},\,-{\frac {\partial }{\partial x_{3}}}\right)\\&amp;=(\partial ^{0},\,-\partial ^{1},\,-\partial ^{2},\,-\partial ^{3})\\&amp;=\mathbf {E} _{0}\partial ^{0}-\mathbf {E} _{1}\partial ^{1}-\mathbf {E} _{2}\partial ^{2}-\mathbf {E} _{3}\partial ^{3}\\&amp;=\mathbf {E} _{0}\partial ^{0}-\mathbf {E} _{i}\partial ^{i}\\&amp;=\mathbf {E} _{\alpha }\partial ^{\alpha }\\&amp;=\left({\frac {1}{c}}{\frac {\partial }{\partial t}},\,-\nabla \right)\\&amp;=\left({\frac {\partial _{t}}{c}},-\nabla \right)\\&amp;=\mathbf {E} _{0}{\frac {1}{c}}{\frac {\partial }{\partial t}}-\nabla \\\end{aligned}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/1c1fddad39445c6b33cbc1b8da24a844aa309b9f" style="vertical-align: -18.171ex; width:36.856ex; height:37.509ex;"/></span></dd>

<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\begin{aligned}{\boldsymbol {\partial }}&amp;=\left({\frac {\partial }{\partial x^{0}}},\,{\frac {\partial }{\partial x^{1}}},\,{\frac {\partial }{\partial x^{2}}},\,{\frac {\partial }{\partial x^{3}}}\right)\\&amp;=(\partial _{0},\,\partial _{1},\,\partial _{2},\,\partial _{3})\\&amp;=\mathbf {E} ^{0}\partial _{0}+\mathbf {E} ^{1}\partial _{1}+\mathbf {E} ^{2}\partial _{2}+\mathbf {E} ^{3}\partial _{3}\\&amp;=\mathbf {E} ^{0}\partial _{0}+\mathbf {E} ^{i}\partial _{i}\\&amp;=\mathbf {E} ^{\alpha }\partial _{\alpha }\\&amp;=\left({\frac {1}{c}}{\frac {\partial }{\partial t}},\,\nabla \right)\\&amp;=\left({\frac {\partial _{t}}{c}},\nabla \right)\\&amp;=\mathbf {E} ^{0}{\frac {1}{c}}{\frac {\partial }{\partial t}}+\nabla \\\end{aligned}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle {\begin{aligned}{\boldsymbol {\partial }}&amp;=\left({\frac {\partial }{\partial x^{0}}},\,{\frac {\partial }{\partial x^{1}}},\,{\frac {\partial }{\partial x^{2}}},\,{\frac {\partial }{\partial x^{3}}}\right)\\&amp;=(\partial _{0},\,\partial _{1},\,\partial _{2},\,\partial _{3})\\&amp;=\mathbf {E} ^{0}\partial _{0}+\mathbf {E} ^{1}\partial _{1}+\mathbf {E} ^{2}\partial _{2}+\mathbf {E} ^{3}\partial _{3}\\&amp;=\mathbf {E} ^{0}\partial _{0}+\mathbf {E} ^{i}\partial _{i}\\&amp;=\mathbf {E} ^{\alpha }\partial _{\alpha }\\&amp;=\left({\frac {1}{c}}{\frac {\partial }{\partial t}},\,\nabla \right)\\&amp;=\left({\frac {\partial _{t}}{c}},\nabla \right)\\&amp;=\mathbf {E} ^{0}{\frac {1}{c}}{\frac {\partial }{\partial t}}+\nabla \\\end{aligned}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/8245ddd6dce59a687d5815aa5416f2d5d4edf85e" style="vertical-align: -18.005ex; width:34.493ex; height:37.176ex;"/></span></dd>
</dl>

<p>called the <a href="/wiki/D%27Alembert_operator" title="D'Alembert operator">D'Alembert operator</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Kinematics">Kinematics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Four-vector&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Kinematics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Four-velocity">Four-velocity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Four-vector&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Four-velocity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Four-acceleration">Four-acceleration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Four-vector&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Four-acceleration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Four-acceleration" title="Four-acceleration">four-acceleration</a> is given by:</p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="bold">A</mi>
</mrow>
<mo>=</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mfrac>
<mrow>
<mi>d</mi>

</mrow>
</mrow>
<mrow>
<mi>d</mi>
<mi>τ<!-- τ --></mi>
</mrow>
</mfrac>

<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>

</mrow>

<mrow>
<mo>(</mo>

<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbf {A} ={\frac {d\mathbf {U} }{d\tau }}=\gamma (\mathbf {u} )\left({\frac {d{\gamma }(\mathbf {u} )}{dt}}c,{\frac {d{\gamma }(\mathbf {u} )}{dt}}\mathbf {u} +\gamma (\mathbf {u} )\mathbf {a} \right).}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbf{A} =\frac{d\mathbf{U} }{d \tau} = \gamma(\mathbf{u}) \left(\frac{d{\gamma}(\mathbf{u})}{dt} c, \frac{d{\gamma}(\mathbf{u})}{dt} \mathbf{u} + \gamma(\mathbf{u}) \mathbf{a} \right)." aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/1f73faa870dfa27859712efa9a2a68e412224957" style="vertical-align: -2.505ex; width:47.489ex; height:6.343ex;"/></span></dd>
</dl>
<p>where <b>a</b> = <i>d</i><b>u</b>/<i>dt</i> is the coordinate 3-acceleration. Since the magnitude of <b>U</b> is a constant, the four acceleration is orthogonal to the four velocity, i.e. the Minkowski inner product of the four-acceleration and the four-velocity is zero:</p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="bold">A</mi>
</mrow>
<mo>⋅<!-- ⋅ --></mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="bold">U</mi>
</mrow>
<mo>=</mo>
<msup>
<mi>A</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>μ<!-- μ --></mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<msub>
<mi>U</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>μ<!-- μ --></mi>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Dynamics">Dynamics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Four-vector&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Dynamics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Four-momentum">Four-momentum</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Four-vector&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Four-momentum">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>For a massive particle of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rest_mass" title="Rest mass">rest mass</a> (or <a href="/wiki/Invariant_mass" title="Invariant mass">invariant mass</a>) <i>m</i><sub>0</sub>, the <a href="/wiki/Four-momentum" title="Four-momentum">four-momentum</a> is given by:</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Four-force">Four-force</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Four-vector&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Four-force">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Four-force" title="Four-force">four-force</a> acting on a particle is defined analogously to the 3-force as the time derivative of 3-momentum in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Newton%27s_second_law" title="Newton's second law">Newton's second law</a>:</p>

<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbf {F} =m_{0}\mathbf {A} =m_{0}\gamma (\mathbf {u} )\left({\frac {d{\gamma }(\mathbf {u} )}{dt}}c,\left({\frac {d{\gamma }(\mathbf {u} )}{dt}}\mathbf {u} +\gamma (\mathbf {u} )\mathbf {a} \right)\right)}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\mathbf  {F}}=m_{0}{\mathbf  {A}}=m_{0}\gamma ({\mathbf  {u}})\left({\frac  {d{\gamma }({\mathbf  {u}})}{dt}}c,\left({\frac  {d{\gamma }({\mathbf  {u}})}{dt}}{\mathbf  {u}}+\gamma ({\mathbf  {u}}){\mathbf  {a}}\right)\right)" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/83a9991f359058ec0dbd0c8a3aa9a70460e8e9ad" style="vertical-align: -2.505ex; width:53.675ex; height:6.343ex;"/></span></dd>
</dl>
<p>An invariant derived from the four-force is:</p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

</mrow>
<mo>⋅<!-- ⋅ --></mo>

<mi mathvariant="bold">U</mi>
</mrow>
<mo>=</mo>

</mrow>
</msup>

<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

<mn>0</mn>
</mrow>

</mrow>

</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\mathbf  {F}}\cdot {\mathbf  {U}}=F^{\mu }U_{\mu }=m_{0}A^{\mu }U_{\mu }=0" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/950fc6108639171a2f0b39b5d97469a544bfd33d" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:30.76ex; height:3.009ex;"/></span></dd>
</dl>
<p>from the above result.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Thermodynamics">Thermodynamics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Four-vector&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Thermodynamics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Relativistic_heat_conduction" title="Relativistic heat conduction">Relativistic heat conduction</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Four-heat_flux">Four-heat flux</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Four-vector&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Four-heat flux">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The four-heat flux vector field, is essentially similar to the 3d <a href="/wiki/Heat_flux" title="Heat flux">heat flux</a> vector field <b>q</b>, in the local frame of the fluid:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="bold">Q</mi>
</mrow>
<mo>=</mo>
<mo>−<!-- − --></mo>
<mi>k</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="bold">∂<!-- ∂ --></mi>
</mrow>
<mi>T</mi>
<mo>=</mo>
<mo>−<!-- − --></mo>
<mi>k</mi>
<mrow>
<mo>(</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mfrac>
<mn>1</mn>
<mi>c</mi>
</mfrac>
</mrow>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mfrac>

</mrow>
</mfrac>
</mrow>

<mi>T</mi>
<mo>)</mo>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbf {Q} =-k{\boldsymbol {\partial }}T=-k\left({\frac {1}{c}}{\frac {\partial T}{\partial t}},\nabla T\right)}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbf{Q} = -k \boldsymbol{\partial} T = - k\left( \frac{1}{c}\frac{\partial T}{\partial t}, \nabla T\right) " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/dbcd3c3fc2219e6825b98ceec635ca50b8246330" style="vertical-align: -2.505ex; width:31.788ex; height:6.176ex;"/></span></dd>
</dl>
<p>where <i>T</i> is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Absolute_temperature" title="Absolute temperature">absolute temperature</a> and <i>k</i> is <a href="/wiki/Thermal_conductivity" title="Thermal conductivity">thermal conductivity</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Four-baryon_number_flux">Four-baryon number flux</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Four-vector&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Four-baryon number flux">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The flux of baryons is:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="bold">S</mi>
</mrow>
<mo>=</mo>
<mi>n</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="bold">U</mi>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbf {S} =n\mathbf {U} }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbf{S}= n\mathbf{U}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a22ff4ce8fd3af10a0eba5e4b9e3d852f6b56cc7" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:8.077ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span></dd>
</dl>
<p>where <i>n</i> is the <a href="/wiki/Number_density" title="Number density">number density</a> of <a href="/wiki/Baryon" title="Baryon">baryons</a> in the local <a href="/wiki/Rest_frame" title="Rest frame">rest frame</a> of the baryon fluid (positive values for baryons, negative for <a href="/wiki/Antiparticle" title="Antiparticle">antibaryons</a>), and <b>U</b> the <a href="/wiki/Four-velocity" title="Four-velocity">four-velocity</a> field (of the fluid) as above.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Four-entropy">Four-entropy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Four-vector&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Four-entropy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The four-<a href="/wiki/Entropy" title="Entropy">entropy</a> vector is defined by:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="bold">s</mi>
</mrow>
<mo>=</mo>
<mi>s</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="bold">S</mi>
</mrow>
<mo>+</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mfrac>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="bold">Q</mi>
</mrow>
<mi>T</mi>
</mfrac>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbf {s} =s\mathbf {S} +{\frac {\mathbf {Q} }{T}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbf{s}= s\mathbf{S} + \frac{\mathbf{Q}}{T}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f84362e6079a6227b32693ab23a05ad101eb661b" style="vertical-align: -1.838ex; width:12.477ex; height:5.343ex;"/></span></dd>
</dl>
<p>where <i>s</i> is the entropy per baryon, and <i>T</i> the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Absolute_temperature" title="Absolute temperature">absolute temperature</a>, in the local rest frame of the fluid.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Electromagnetism">Electromagnetism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Four-vector&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Electromagnetism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Examples of four-vectors in <a href="/wiki/Electromagnetism" title="Electromagnetism">electromagnetism</a> include the following.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Four-current">Four-current</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Four-vector&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Four-current">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The electromagnetic <a href="/wiki/Four-current" title="Four-current">four-current</a> (or more correctly a four-current density)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> is defined by</p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="bold">J</mi>
</mrow>
<mo>=</mo>
<mrow>
<mo>(</mo>
<mi>ρ<!-- ρ --></mi>
<mi>c</mi>
<mo>,</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="bold">j</mi>
</mrow>
<mo>)</mo>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbf {J} =\left(\rho c,\mathbf {j} \right)}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt=" \mathbf{J} = \left( \rho c, \mathbf{j} \right) " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/20f1b6e950be58af096c8645f49a9efd37aa3bb0" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:10.431ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span></dd>
</dl>
<p>formed from the <a href="/wiki/Current_density" title="Current density">current density</a> <b>j</b> and <a href="/wiki/Charge_density" title="Charge density">charge density</a> <i>ρ</i>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Four-potential">Four-potential</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Four-vector&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Four-potential">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Waves">Waves</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Four-vector&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Waves">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Four-frequency">Four-frequency</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Four-vector&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Four-frequency">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A photonic <a href="/wiki/Plane_wave" title="Plane wave">plane wave</a> can be described by the <a href="/wiki/Four-frequency" title="Four-frequency">four-frequency</a> defined as</p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="bold">N</mi>
</mrow>
<mo>=</mo>
<mi>ν<!-- ν --></mi>
<mrow>
<mo>(</mo>
<mn>1</mn>
<mo>,</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mover>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="bold">n</mi>
</mrow>
<mo stretchy="false">^<!-- ^ --></mo>
</mover>
</mrow>
</mrow>
<mo>)</mo>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbf {N} =\nu \left(1,{\hat {\mathbf {n} }}\right)}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbf{N} = \nu\left(1 , \hat{\mathbf{n}} \right)" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/2328109b8609e4b3d287737f94867fb98c3b16d4" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:12.384ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span></dd>
</dl>
<p>where <i>ν</i> is the frequency of the wave and <span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mover>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="bold">n</mi>
</mrow>
<mo stretchy="false">^<!-- ^ --></mo>
</mover>
</mrow>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\hat {\mathbf {n} }}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\hat {\mathbf {n} }}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/aae87b164ba005e99b51066c46d1eacc7f56564a" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.496ex; height:2.343ex;"/></span> is a <a href="/wiki/Unit_vector" title="Unit vector">unit vector</a> in the travel direction of the wave. Now:</p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mo fence="false" stretchy="false">∥<!-- ∥ --></mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="bold">N</mi>
</mrow>
<mo>∥<!-- ∥ --></mo>
<mo>=</mo>
<msup>
<mi>N</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>μ<!-- μ --></mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<msub>
<mi>N</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>μ<!-- μ --></mi>
</mrow>
</msub>

</semantics>
</math></span><img alt=" \|\mathbf{N}\| = N^\mu N_\mu = \nu ^2 \left(1 - \hat{\mathbf{n}}\cdot\hat{\mathbf{n}}\right) = 0 " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0cd1bfc28369661bcebf385684173cfa07bfef1b" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:34.671ex; height:3.343ex;"/></span></dd>

<p>so the four-frequency of a photon is always a null vector.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Four-wavevector">Four-wavevector</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Four-vector&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Four-wavevector">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/De_Broglie_relation" title="De Broglie relation">De Broglie relation</a></div>
<p>The quantities reciprocal to time <i>t</i> and space <b>r</b> are the <a href="/wiki/Angular_frequency" title="Angular frequency">angular frequency</a> <i>ω</i> and <a href="/wiki/Wave_vector" title="Wave vector">wave vector</a> <b>k</b>, respectively. They form the components of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Four-wavevector" title="Four-wavevector">four-wavevector</a> or wave four-vector:</p>

<p>or ||<b>k</b>|| = <i>ω</i>/<i>c</i>. Note this is consistent with the above case; for photons with a 3-wavevector of modulus <i>ω</i>/<i>c</i>, in the direction of wave propagation defined by the unit vector <span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\hat {\mathbf {n} }}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\hat {\mathbf {n} }}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/aae87b164ba005e99b51066c46d1eacc7f56564a" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.496ex; height:2.343ex;"/></span>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Quantum_theory">Quantum theory</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Four-vector&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Quantum theory">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Four-probability_current">Four-probability current</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Four-vector&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Four-probability current">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Quantum_mechanics" title="Quantum mechanics">quantum mechanics</a>, the four-<a href="/wiki/Probability_current" title="Probability current">probability current</a> or probability four-current is analogous to the electromagnetic four-current:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="bold">J</mi>
</mrow>
<mo>=</mo>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mi>ρ<!-- ρ --></mi>
<mi>c</mi>
<mo>,</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="bold">j</mi>
</mrow>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbf {J} =(\rho c,\mathbf {j} )}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbf{J} = (\rho c, \mathbf{j}) " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/34b9c82155c9e5e200d6b1c0649c78177b285114" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:10.431ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span></dd>
</dl>
<p>where <i>ρ</i> is the <a href="/wiki/Probability_density_function" title="Probability density function">probability density function</a> corresponding to the time component, and <b>j</b> is the <a href="/wiki/Probability_current" title="Probability current">probability current</a> vector. In non-relativistic quantum mechanics, this current is always well defined because the expressions for density and current are positive definite and can admit a probability interpretation. In <a href="/wiki/Relativistic_quantum_mechanics" title="Relativistic quantum mechanics">relativistic quantum mechanics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Quantum_field_theory" title="Quantum field theory">quantum field theory</a>, it is not always possible to find a current, particularly when interactions are involved.</p>
<p>Replacing the energy by the <a href="/wiki/Energy_operator" title="Energy operator">energy operator</a> and the momentum by the <a href="/wiki/Momentum_operator" title="Momentum operator">momentum operator</a> in the four-momentum, one obtains the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Four-momentum_operator" title="Four-momentum operator">four-momentum operator</a>, used in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Relativistic_wave_equation" title="Relativistic wave equation">relativistic wave equations</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Four-spin">Four-spin</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Four-vector&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Four-spin">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Four-spin" title="Four-spin">four-spin</a> of a particle is defined in the rest frame of a particle to be</p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="bold">S</mi>
</mrow>
<mo>=</mo>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mn>0</mn>
<mo>,</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="bold">s</mi>
</mrow>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbf {S} =(0,\mathbf {s} )}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle \mathbf {S} =(0,\mathbf {s} )}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/dfd7676115f3c06a9d4e6c0c3ea1302edb55c73d" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:9.718ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span></dd>
</dl>
<p>where <b>s</b> is the <a href="/wiki/Spin_(physics)" title="Spin (physics)">spin</a> pseudovector. In quantum mechanics, not all three components of this vector are simultaneously measurable, only one component is. The timelike component is zero in the particle's rest frame, but not in any other frame. This component can be found from an appropriate Lorentz transformation.</p>
<p>The norm squared is the (negative of the) magnitude squared of the spin, and according to quantum mechanics we have</p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mo fence="false" stretchy="false">∥<!-- ∥ --></mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="bold">S</mi>
</mrow>
<msup>
<mo>∥<!-- ∥ --></mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>2</mn>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>=</mo>
<mo>−<!-- − --></mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo stretchy="false">|</mo>
</mrow>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="bold">s</mi>
</mrow>
<msup>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo stretchy="false">|</mo>
</mrow>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>2</mn>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>=</mo>
<mo>−<!-- − --></mo>
<msup>
<mi class="MJX-variant">ℏ<!-- ℏ --></mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>2</mn>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mi>s</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mi>s</mi>
<mo>+</mo>
<mn>1</mn>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \|\mathbf {S} \|^{2}=-|\mathbf {s} |^{2}=-\hbar ^{2}s(s+1)}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle \|\mathbf {S} \|^{2}=-|\mathbf {s} |^{2}=-\hbar ^{2}s(s+1)}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/90e2b3625b5ce90dae647a9f6d5172ea8745f50a" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:28.65ex; height:3.343ex;"/></span></dd>
</dl>
<p>This value is observable and quantized, with <i>s</i> the <a href="/wiki/Spin_quantum_number" title="Spin quantum number">spin quantum number</a> (not the magnitude of the spin vector).</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_formulations">Other formulations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Four-vector&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Other formulations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Four-vectors_in_the_algebra_of_physical_space">Four-vectors in the algebra of physical space</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Four-vector&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Four-vectors in the algebra of physical space">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<p>and in this formulation, the four-vector is represented as a <a href="/wiki/Hermitian_matrix" title="Hermitian matrix">Hermitian matrix</a> (the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Matrix_transpose" title="Matrix transpose">matrix transpose</a> and <a href="/wiki/Complex_conjugate" title="Complex conjugate">complex conjugate</a> of the matrix leaves it unchanged), rather than a real-valued column or row vector. The <a href="/wiki/Determinant" title="Determinant">determinant</a> of the matrix is the modulus of the four-vector, so the determinant is an invariant:</p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mtable columnalign="right left right left right left right left right left right left" columnspacing="0em 2em 0em 2em 0em 2em 0em 2em 0em 2em 0em" displaystyle="true" rowspacing="3pt">
<mtr>
<mtd>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo stretchy="false">|</mo>
</mrow>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi mathvariant="bold">A</mi>
</mrow>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo stretchy="false">|</mo>
</mrow>
</mtd>
<mtd>
<mi></mi>
<mo>=</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mrow>
