<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\begin{aligned}|\mathbf {A} |&amp;={\begin{vmatrix}A^{0}+A^{3}&amp;A^{1}-iA^{2}\\A^{1}+iA^{2}&amp;A^{0}-A^{3}\end{vmatrix}}\\&amp;=(A^{0}+A^{3})(A^{0}-A^{3})-(A^{1}-iA^{2})(A^{1}+iA^{2})\\&amp;=(A^{0})^{2}-(A^{1})^{2}-(A^{2})^{2}-(A^{3})^{2}\end{aligned}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt=" \begin{align}  
|\mathbf{A}| &amp; = \begin{vmatrix} A^0 + A^3 &amp; A^1 -i A^2 \\ A^1 + i A^2 &amp; A^0 - A^3 \end{vmatrix} \\
&amp; = (A^0 + A^3)(A^0 - A^3)  - (A^1 -i A^2)(A^1 + i A^2) \\
&amp; = (A^0)^2 - (A^1)^2 - (A^2)^2 - (A^3)^2
\end{align}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/6871cd6381b78cfe994d28273e5fb33b751f1a27" style="vertical-align: -6.005ex; width:52.927ex; height:13.009ex;"/></span></dd>
</dl>
<p>This idea of using the Pauli matrices as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Basis_vector" title="Basis vector">basis vectors</a> is employed in the <a href="/wiki/Algebra_of_physical_space" title="Algebra of physical space">algebra of physical space</a>, an example of a <a href="/wiki/Clifford_algebra" title="Clifford algebra">Clifford algebra</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Four-vectors_in_spacetime_algebra">Four-vectors in spacetime algebra</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Four-vector&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Four-vectors in spacetime algebra">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Spacetime_algebra" title="Spacetime algebra">spacetime algebra</a>, another example of Clifford algebra, the <a href="/wiki/Gamma_matrices" title="Gamma matrices">gamma matrices</a> can also form a <a href="/wiki/Basis_(linear_algebra)" title="Basis (linear algebra)">basis</a>. (They are also called the Dirac matrices, owing to their appearance in the <a href="/wiki/Dirac_equation" title="Dirac equation">Dirac equation</a>). There is more than one way to express the gamma matrices, detailed in that main article.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Feynman_slash_notation" title="Feynman slash notation">Feynman slash notation</a> is a shorthand for a four-vector <b>A</b> contracted with the gamma matrices:</p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbf {A} \!\!\!\!/=A_{\alpha }\gamma ^{\alpha }=A_{0}\gamma ^{0}+A_{1}\gamma ^{1}+A_{2}\gamma ^{2}+A_{3}\gamma ^{3}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\mathbf{A}\!\!\!\!/ = A_\alpha \gamma^\alpha = A_0 \gamma^0 + A_1 \gamma^1 + A_2 \gamma^2 + A_3 \gamma^3 " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b7a4e4e99b9cc73b39e90afbbe7491d04c6e14d4" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:42.72ex; height:3.176ex;"/></span></dd>
</dl>
<p>The four-momentum contracted with the gamma matrices is an important case in <a href="/wiki/Relativistic_quantum_mechanics" title="Relativistic quantum mechanics">relativistic quantum mechanics</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Relativistic_quantum_field_theory" title="Relativistic quantum field theory">relativistic quantum field theory</a>. In the Dirac equation and other <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Relativistic_wave_equation" title="Relativistic wave equation">relativistic wave equations</a>, terms of the form:</p>

<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbf {P} \!\!\!\!/=P_{\alpha }\gamma ^{\alpha }=P_{0}\gamma ^{0}+P_{1}\gamma ^{1}+P_{2}\gamma ^{2}+P_{3}\gamma ^{3}={\dfrac {E}{c}}\gamma ^{0}-p_{x}\gamma ^{1}-p_{y}\gamma ^{2}-p_{z}\gamma ^{3}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\mathbf  {P}}\!\!\!\!/=P_{\alpha }\gamma ^{\alpha }=P_{0}\gamma ^{0}+P_{1}\gamma ^{1}+P_{2}\gamma ^{2}+P_{3}\gamma ^{3}={\dfrac  {E}{c}}\gamma ^{0}-p_{x}\gamma ^{1}-p_{y}\gamma ^{2}-p_{z}\gamma ^{3}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/dfe18c4998baa5dcef69f58855374b800d04d4f6" style="vertical-align: -1.838ex; width:71.75ex; height:5.343ex;"/></span></dd>
</dl>
<p>appear, in which the energy <i>E</i> and momentum components <span class="nowrap">(<i>p<sub>x</sub></i>, <i>p<sub>y</sub></i>, <i>p<sub>z</sub></i>)</span> are replaced by their respective <a href="/wiki/Operator_(physics)" title="Operator (physics)">operators</a>.</p>
